                .addSize([0, 0], [640, 480])
                .build()
        };

        gptPage = window.digitalData && digitalData.page && digitalData.page.page ? digitalData.page.page : "blank";
        gptSubPage = window.digitalData && digitalData.page && digitalData.page.subPage ? digitalData.page.subPage : "blank";

        function gptClean(gptText) {
            if (typeof (gptText) == "string") {
                gptText = gptText.replace(/\&/g, '%26');
                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

        googletag.pubads()
            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send
            .setTargeting('doi', gptClean('10.1002/adfm.202405460')) // Publication DOI
            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

        googletag.defineSlot($GooglePublisherCategory, 'fluid', 'advert-leaderboard')
            .defineSizeMapping(sizes.leaderboard)
            .addService(googletag.pubads())
            .setCollapseEmptyDiv(true);

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="dd3c4fbf1d404c52ad279918d569db9e">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '284db039-ec98-407a-9d33-833bec9adad7'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d107712298" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>As a promising anode material for Na-metal batteries, the practical application of Na metal is severely hindered due to the formation of the notorious dendrite and unstable solid-electrolyte interface (SEI). To address these issues, a direct-ink writing (DIW) 3D printing technology is proposed to construct an artificial 3D hierarchical porous sodiophilic Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/reduced graphene-oxide (Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO) aerogel monolith, which is employed as the matrix of Na metal anode. Benefiting from the homogeneous ion flux and exceptional sodiophilic features, the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes embedded within the 3D scaffold regulate the uniform deposition of metallic Na with a stable SEI layer, achieving an ultralong cycle lifespan of 3000&nbsp;h at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> and an impressive Coulombic efficiency of 99.68% over extended lifespan of 7064&nbsp;h. Further, the in-depth characterization analysis proves that the formed stable SEI layer consists of an inorganic NaF accumulated in the inner layer and loosely-bound organic species in the outer layer. Remarkably, when integrated into a Na metal full cell, the reversible capacity reaches 90.22 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles at 100&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. The work provides a promising strategy to utilize Na metal anodes with long cycle lifespan for next-generation sodium metal batteries.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202405460-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202405460-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>To meet the ever-increasing demands for low cost with large energy density rechargeable power source in electronics, electric vehicles, and smart grid storage systems, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) utilizing advanced electrodes have been rapidly explored as high performance energy storage systems.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0001_R_d107712164e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Energy">1</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0003_R_d107712164e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Energy Mater.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sodium (Na) metal, as one of the most promising anode materials of SIBs, has garnered substantial attention due to its large theoretical specific capacity, low redox plateau and abundant resources.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0004_R_d107712164e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Energy">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0005_R_d107712164e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the practical implementation of metallic sodium anodes are still facing formidable challenges, including the formation of uncontrollable dendrites, infinite volume expansion, inferior Coulombic efficiency (CE), and rapid capacity degradation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0004_R_d107712164e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Energy">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0006_R_d107712164e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Chem">6</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0007_R_d107712164e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Environ. Sci.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Extensive efforts have been devoted to addressing these issues through proposed approaches, such as electrolyte modification, artificial interface engineering, alloy design, and construction of 3D nanostructured scaffolds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0008_R_d107712164e541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">8</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0016_R_d107712164e541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Joule">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the application of a 3D porous structure adorned with a sodiophilic matrix is considered to be a practical solution to impede dendrite formation, prolong the dendrite nucleation time, and promote homogeneous deposition of sodium metal.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0009_R_d107712164e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Mater.">9</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0017_R_d107712164e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Energy Storage Mater.">17</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0018_R_d107712164e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Energy Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>MXene, as a new emerged group of 2D materials, has been explored to improve the electrochemical performance of sodium metal anode by virtue of their native hydrophilic surface, superb conductivity, good chemical stability and surface engineering flexibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0019_R_d107712164e553" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - ACS Nano">19</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0022_R_d107712164e553" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Energy Environ. Sci.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Recent studies have reported on the utilization of MXene (Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>, V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>) and related derivates to construct the hosts for Na metal anodes, such as 3D porous Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>-reduced graphene oxide (Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>-rGO) membrane, 3D printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-carbon nanotube (CNT) microgrid aerogel and 3D printed Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) microgrid aerogels.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0023_R_d107712164e593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - ACS Nano">23</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0025_R_d107712164e593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nanoscale">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For instance, a superior cycling life &gt; 3000&nbsp;h with an average CE of 99.54% at 2&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>, 10 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> was achieved by utilizing V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-CNT as electrodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0025_R_d107712164e607" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nanoscale">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Recently research efforts have been paid to Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub>, V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> and their hybrid structures. However, there is limited exploration of other new MXenes as the matrices for Na metal anodes. Furthermore, rare investigations have been conducted on the formation and properties of the solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) layer with MXene-based Na metal anodes. Therefore, it is urgent to develop alternative MXene-derived hybrid structures as potential hosts and to advance our understandings of the Na deposition behavior on such matrices.</p>
         
         <p>Among diverse materials in MXene family, Nb<sub>2</sub>C has been investigated for a variety of applications, including photodetectors, lithium-ion batteries and lithium-oxygen batteries.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0026_R_d107712164e628" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - ACS Nano">26</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0029_R_d107712164e628" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Environ. Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Herein, Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> is selected as the host of the Na metal anodes owing to the large capacity due to the only three atomic layers and high electrochemical activity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0030_R_d107712164e638" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv. Mater.">30</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0031_R_d107712164e638" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - ACS Nano">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In this work, an artificial Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO microgrid aerogel monolith was fabricated by a direct-ink writing (DIW) 3D printing technology. This 3D printed Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO (3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO) electrode shows excellent performance as a superior scaffold for Na metal anodes with featured key advantages. First, 3D printed aerogel monoliths provide a large specific surface area which can effectively reduce the current density of the electrode surface, and abundant Na metal nucleation sites. Second, the artificial hierarchical porous architecture created by 3D printing process promotes effective electrolyte penetration, ensuring close contact between electrolyte and the electrodes. Additionally, this structure effectively improves the ion diffusion coefficient and alleviates volume expansion of electrode, thus leading to electrochemical stability enhancement. Thirdly, the sodiophilic Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene nanoflakes exhibit sodiophilic character, which enhances the nucleation and deposition stability of Na ions. Fourthly, a robust and stable SEI layer consisted of inorganic NaF species accumulated in the inner layer and loosely-bound organic species in the outer layer is formed at the interface between the electrolyte and Na metal anodes with the assistant of sodiophilic Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes. With these advantages, the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode can be stably operated longer than 3000&nbsp;h at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> when measured in symmetric cell. In addition, it also retains a high average CE of 99.68% over significantly extended cycle lifespan of 7064&nbsp;h at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. Furthermore, a full cell assembled with a 3D printed Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C/rGO (3DP NVP@C/rGO) cathode and the Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO anode demonstrates a highly reversible specific capacity of 90.22 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a small per-cycle decay of 0.009% at a current density of 100&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. Our work provides valuable insights into the advancement of sodiophilic Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO monoliths electrode to significantly enhance the cycling stability of Na metal anodes by the usage of advanced 3D printing technology.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202405460-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202405460-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p><b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0001">1</a> shows the fabrication process of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO aerogel structure. Initially, the interlayer of Al atoms was etched away from the Nb<sub>2</sub>AlC MAX phase to form accordion-like multilayer Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Then, the interlayer distance of the multilayer Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> was enlarged by the intercalation of tetrapropylammonium hydroxide (TPAOH), followed by exfoliating to single-layer or few-layer Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes by ultrasonic irradiation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0027_R_d107712164e735" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Nano">27</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0028_R_d107712164e735" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Then the sample was freeze-dried to obtain the powder, and re-dispersed into the water to prepare the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> solution with a fixed concentration. During this process, numerous ─OH and ─F functional groups are formed on the surface of the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene nanoflakes, which imparts hydrophilicity and sodiophilicity characters. Our Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes with an average size of ≈250&nbsp;nm were used as the sodiophilic material incorporated with the rGO as the skeleton to support the Na metal anodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). The Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes and GO nanoflakes with various mass ratios were physically homogeneously mixed with each other under continuous stirring, followed by centrifugation to remove the excess water to get the gel-like 3D printable ink. The ink was directly printed on a glass substrate, followed by freeze-drying and annealing to finally attain the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO aerogel. It is worth mentioning that it is convenient to print the with the designed patterns and size by 3D printing technology. For example, a snowflake pattern, characters of “NBC”, and “20 layers stairway” structures (front-view and top-view, the dimensions of each four layers vary from 0.4 × 0.4 to 2.0 × 2.0&nbsp;cm from top to bottom) were easily printed onto a glass substrate (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). In addition, the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO aerogels also exhibit ultra-light character supported by a dandelion (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, the 3D printed electrodes also show good wetting properties with the electrolyte. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information), 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes with 1, 4, and 8 layers could be easily wetted with 75&nbsp;µL electrolyte. Even an ultra-thick electrode with 24 layers could be completely wetted by 200&nbsp;µL electrolyte. In this work, a four-layer 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO microlattice with a size of 1.0 × 1.0&nbsp;cm and thickness of 2.0&nbsp;mm (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information) was fabricated for further characterization and electrochemical performance evaluation.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202405460-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/bf6fa1a9-50ea-490b-93fe-e7f262453889/adfm202405460-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/bf6fa1a9-50ea-490b-93fe-e7f262453889/adfm202405460-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/750cc769-7795-4790-99e2-e11e9632f51e/adfm202405460-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/bf6fa1a9-50ea-490b-93fe-e7f262453889/adfm202405460-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202405460-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202405460" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>

                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic diagram of the fabrication process of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO microlattice aerogel electrode.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The morphology of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 aerogel monolith is shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2a–e</a>. 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode is a grid-like arrangement of filaments with an average diameter of ≈450&nbsp;µm interwoven vertically (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2a</a>), along with numerous micropores and medium pores through the filament with an average diameter of ≈25&nbsp;µm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2b</a>). Notably, Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes with lateral size ranging from 30 to 300&nbsp;nm are uniformly decorated on the surface of the rGO sheets (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2c</a>). The bare 3DP rGO and other Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO aerogel electrodes exhibit similar morphology as the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 aerogel as witnessed in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7–S9</a> (Supporting Information). Furthermore, transmission electron microscopy (TEM) image verifies that the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes are randomly stacked on rGO nanosheets (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2d</a>). The high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) exhibits the crystal facial spacing of 0.34 and 0.27&nbsp;nm, attributed to the (002) and (100) crystal lattice of rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2e</a>). The elements of C, O, F and Nb are homogeneously distributed over the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2f</a>. From the X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2g</a>, a sharp characteristic peak at ≈26.2° corresponds to the (002) crystal plane of rGO.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0032_R_d107712164e883" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - J. Mater. Chem. A">32</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0033_R_d107712164e883" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Mater. Chem. A">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO, there is new diffraction peak emerged centered at 7.6°, which is a characteristic peak belonging to the crystal lattice of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> (JCPDS No. 15–0127).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0019_R_d107712164e897" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - ACS Nano">19</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0029_R_d107712164e897" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Environ. Mater.">29</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0034_R_d107712164e897" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Ceram. Int.">34</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0035_R_d107712164e897" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nano Energy">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The 3D-printed samples were further characterized by Raman spectra (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). For all samples, there are two peaks centered at 1350 and 1580 cm<sup>−1</sup>, attributed to disordered induced D-band and in-plane vibration of sp<sup>2</sup> carbon atoms G-band of rGO, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0036_R_d107712164e910" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Energy Storage Mater.">36</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0037_R_d107712164e910" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Carbon">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The peaks in 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO centered at 120.8 and 251.6 cm<sup>−1</sup> can be attributed to Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene. In addition, two peaks located at 652.5 and 973.9 cm<sup>−1</sup> can be attributed to Nb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> due to the oxidation of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene during the fabrication process, which is commonly observed in previous reports.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0027_R_d107712164e937" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Nano">27</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0038_R_d107712164e937" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - ChemSusChem">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202405460-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ab047174-3956-4301-8700-5e9c243753b2/adfm202405460-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/ab047174-3956-4301-8700-5e9c243753b2/adfm202405460-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/25ef4e18-7f91-4711-ad76-1db53ae02eee/adfm202405460-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ab047174-3956-4301-8700-5e9c243753b2/adfm202405460-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202405460-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202405460" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>

                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Characterization of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes. Inset in e) is the related selected area electron diffration (SAED)&nbsp;pattern. f) The EDS elemental mapping of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 microlattice aerogel. g) XRD patterns of the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene, 3DP rGO, and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO nanocomposites. h) XPS of the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO nanocomposites. i) TGA curves of the 3DP rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO nanocomposites with various ratios.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The chemical valance states of pure Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> and 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO samples were further elucidated by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2h</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). There is a peak located at 684.1&nbsp;eV attributed to the F signal (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2h</a>). In Nb 3d spectrum of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>, there are three peaks at 209.9, 206.8, and 203.9&nbsp;eV, which are assigned to Nb 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, Nb 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and Nb─C, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11a,d</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0029_R_d107712164e1033" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Environ. Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The spectrum of C 1s is composed of five peaks located at 288.74, 286.57, 284.6, 282.9, and 281.5&nbsp;eV, which can be indexed O─C═O, C─O, C─C, Nb─C, and Nb-C<sup>V</sup> (carbon near vacant or defective sites), respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11b,e</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0028_R_d107712164e1044" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0030_R_d107712164e1044" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv. Mater.">30</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0035_R_d107712164e1044" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nano Energy">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the disappearance of Nb-C<sup>V</sup> peak in Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO indicates that the defects in 281.5&nbsp;eV are reduced during the heat treatment process (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11e</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0028_R_d107712164e1059" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the high-resolution O 1s spectrum, there are three peaks centered on 529.3, 531.7, and 530.2&nbsp;eV corresponding to Nb─O, C─Nb─O, C─Nb─OH (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11c,f</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0028_R_d107712164e1067" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These results suggest that the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene contains abundant fluorine and oxygen-containing functional groups (─F, ─OH, and ─O) generated during the HF etching treatment process, which is in good agreement with previous reports.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0027_R_d107712164e1077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Nano">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Thermal gravimetric analyzer (TGA) was used to determine the percentage of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> in the printed aerogel (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0002">2i</a>). The weight loss below 100 °C and 100–530 °C is due to the evaporation of absorbed moisture, and oxidation of rGO, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0039_R_d107712164e1092" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Energy Mater.">39</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0040_R_d107712164e1092" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Sci. Rep.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The slight weight increase of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes after 569&nbsp;°C may be attributed to the mild oxidation of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> and its partial conversion to Nb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0041_R_d107712164e1111" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Power Sources">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, the ratios of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> in 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-10, 30, 50 samples are 11.00%, 26.48%, and 40.98%, respectively, which are basically consistent with the initial ratio. Moreover, the specific surface areas of the 3DP rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-10, 30, 50 electrodes are 343.96, 191.80, 136.36, and 93.16 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information), with the corresponding pore sizes of 4.08, 7.78, 9.61, and 10.01&nbsp;nm, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information). The decrease of the specific surface area with increasing Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> ratios is mainly attributed to the addition of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0042_R_d107712164e1148" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Nano">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>The electrochemical performance of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode was evaluated based on the symmetric cell composed of two Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes fabricated via the electrodeposition of 6 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> Na into the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode. The rate capability of the Na, Na@rGO and Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes was measured with a fixed capacity of 1.0 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at different current densities (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3a</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information). The 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrode shows the optimal rate performance with the most stable and minimum voltage polarizations. As depicts in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), the voltage polarization is reduced with the increase of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> rations, which is assigned to the incorporation of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> which can effectively improve the sodiophilicity of the electrodes with lower nucleation overpotentials and polarizations. However, the polarization of Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-50 symmetric cell is worse than that of Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 cell, which could be attributed to the lower surface area of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-50 than that of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30. Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 not only shows the excellent rate performance, but also exhibits long cycle life span with a small voltage polarization. For example, at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with a fixed capacity of 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, the Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrode exhibits a long cycle lifespan of 3000&nbsp;h, and a small voltage polarization of 62&nbsp;mV even at 2900&nbsp;h of operation (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3b</a>). In contrast, Na, Na@rGO, Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-10 and Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-50 electrodes can cycle for 62, 800, 2800, and 2400&nbsp;h at the same condition (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), respectively. Taken the Na electrode as an example, it shows a stationary voltage polarization in the initial cycle. However, the voltage polarization gradually increases at 64&nbsp;h of operation and then shorts circuit. This can be explained by the uneven deposition of unstable Na formation, which further induced dendrites formation with cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0042_R_d107712164e1251" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Nano">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It is worth mentioning that at a high current density of 6&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 6 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, the Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 symmetric cell also could stably operate for 1100&nbsp;h (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3c</a>). Additionally, we conducted a comparative analysis of the electrochemical performance of the representative MXene electrodes for Na metal anodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0023_R_d107712164e1274" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - ACS Nano">23</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0025_R_d107712164e1274" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nanoscale">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0043_R_d107712164e1274" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - ACS Nano">43</a>-<a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0050_R_d107712164e1274" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - ACS Nano">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The findings indicate that our designed 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes demonstrate exceptional performance, particularly in terms of outstanding long-term cycling stability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202405460-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f9b547ce-5045-4082-9039-01202b680d95/adfm202405460-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f9b547ce-5045-4082-9039-01202b680d95/adfm202405460-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/2218dac5-1317-4e83-8a6e-17553f191252/adfm202405460-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f9b547ce-5045-4082-9039-01202b680d95/adfm202405460-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202405460-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202405460" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance evaluation of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO microlattice aerogel electrodes. a) Rate performance of Na, 3DP Na@rGO and Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 symmetric cell at various current densities. Long-term cycling performances of Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 symmetric cell at b) 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, and c) 6&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 6 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. d) CEs of the Cu, 3DP rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-10, 30, 50 electrodes at 1.0&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1.0 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. e) Voltage profiles of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrode at various current densities based on the half cell. f) EIS curves of the Cu, 3DP rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrodes after 30 cycles. g) Tafel curves of Na@Cu, Na@rGO, and Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrodes to measure the exchange current density.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>As a key indicator for evaluating the reversibility of Na deposition/stripping performance, CE is evaluated utilizing a half cell composed of Cu, 3DP rGO, or Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO as working electrode, and a piece of Na foil as counter electrode. As indicated from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3d</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Supporting Information), the initial CEs of Cu, 3DP rGO, Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-10, 30, 50 electrodes are 26.41%, 44.39%, 96.24%, 100% and 94.22%, respectively. At 1.0&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1.0 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrode exhibits a relatively high average CE of 99.68% for as long as 3532 cycles (7064&nbsp;h, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3d</a>). The 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>C/rGO-50 electrode shows a lower CE of 99.33% and short circuits after 2267&nbsp;h (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>, Supporting Information). The 3DP rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-10 electrodes show large fluctuations of CEs after 800 and 1690&nbsp;h cycles, respectively. In addition to CE, nucleation overpotential is also measured based on the half cell. The Na nucleation overpotentials on the prepared electrodes are measured at 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 4.0, 5.0, and 8.0&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with a fixed capacity of 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3e</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information), respectively, and further explored in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information). It is clearly seen that, at all measured current densities, 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrode exhibits the lowest nucleation overpotentials. It is also found that the nucleation overpotential is reduced with the assistance of the incorporation of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes. Therefore, the function of the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> can effectively reduce the hetero-nucleation energy barriers. All the above electrochemical performance evaluation results indicate that the designed Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrode exhibits the optimal performance among various 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO. Based on the above, further measurement and investigation of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes were performed based on 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrodes.</p>
         
         <p>The diffusion kinetic behaviors of Na ions on Cu, 3DP rGO, and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes were measured based on the charge transfer resistance (<i>R<sub>ct</sub></i>), diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i>) and exchange current density. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3f</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information) show the electrochemical impedance spectrum (EIS) of the prepared Cu, 3DP rGO, and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 electrodes based on the half cells after 30 cycles and the corresponding equivalent circuit, respectively. The fitted values are shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). The <i>R<sub>ct</sub></i> of the Cu, 3DP rGO and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes is decreased from 4370, 1462, and 134 Ω to 3517, 46, and 36 Ω, respectively. The 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode not only has the smallest <i>R<sub>ct</sub></i> both before and after cycles, but also exhibits the most stable <i>R<sub>ct</sub></i> compared to that of the other two electrodes. Moreover, the Na ion diffusion coefficient can be calculated based on the slope of the curve over <i>Z<sub>w</sub></i> and <i>ω<sup>−1/2</sup></i>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0051_R_d107712164e1487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energy Environ. Sci.">51</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0052_R_d107712164e1487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Electrochem. Commun.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Accordingly, Na ion diffusion coefficient of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode is as high as 9.54 × 10<sup>−14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information), which is superior to that of 3DP rGO (7.25 × 10<sup>−14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) and Cu (3.59 × 10<sup>−18</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) electrodes (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, the exchange current density was calculated through Tafel curve measurement as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0003">3g</a>. The 3DP Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode exhibits the highest exchange current density of 4.898&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> compared to that of the Na@rGO (1.237&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) and Na@Cu (0.679&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) electrodes. These results demonstrate that the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode has superior surface kinetics, including low <i>R<sub>ct</sub></i> and large diffusion coefficient, resulting in high-rate capability and long cycle lifespan.</p>
         
         <p>To elucidate the excellent electrochemical performance mechanism of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode, Na deposition morphology, current distribution over the surface of the electrode, the binding energy between Na ions and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes, and SEI composition were further investigated by various in situ/ex situ characterizations from different scales and levels. In detail, the evolution of Na deposition morphology onto Cu, 3DP rGO, and 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes was carried out by an in situ optical microscope at 3&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>. The images were captured from 0 to 120&nbsp;min of deposition as displayed in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4a–c</a>. The Na dendrites (indicated by the dotted yellow arrows) are started to nucleate and grown on Cu and 3DP rGO electrodes after 20 and 40&nbsp;min of deposition, respectively. Due to the “tip effect”, the dendrites attract more Na ions, thus continuously grow larger and larger with the deposition duration.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0053_R_d107712164e1575" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - J. Mater. Chem. A">53</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0054_R_d107712164e1575" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Nat. Commun.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> On the contrary, Na is uniform deposited onto the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode without dendrite formation during the 120&nbsp;min of deposition. It is worth mentioning that bubbles are generated on both the Cu and 3DP rGO electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4a,b</a>), indicating serious side reactions between Na metal and electrolyte due to an unstable SEI layer. Similar phenomenon has also been reported in the previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0055_R_d107712164e1588" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">55</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0056_R_d107712164e1588" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Small">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode maintains a dendrite-free morphology without bubble formation, signifying its exceptional interface stability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202405460-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/baaa8e3c-d2ce-4840-91b9-54c741e42ddb/adfm202405460-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/baaa8e3c-d2ce-4840-91b9-54c741e42ddb/adfm202405460-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/78a6fad6-4d54-4a43-9dc4-72049a0df434/adfm202405460-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/baaa8e3c-d2ce-4840-91b9-54c741e42ddb/adfm202405460-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202405460-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202405460" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">In situ optical microscopy images of Na deposited on a) Cu, b) 3DP rGO, and c) 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes at 3.0&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> for 120&nbsp;min. The current density distribution at the surface of d) Cu, e) 3DP rGO, and f) 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes. Binding energies between g) Nb<sub>2</sub>CF and h) Nb<sub>2</sub>CO with Na calculated by DFT simulation. i) Na metal deposition dynamics upon Nb<sub>2</sub>CO-Na obtained by AIMD simulation.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In addition to investigate the Na deposition morphology from the sub-millimeter scale, the Na deposition/stripping behavior was further investigated by examining the surface morphology evolution of the Cu, 3DP rGO, and 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> by ex situ SEM from micrometer scale (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24–S26</a>, Supporting Information). For the Cu electrode, there are some mossy-like Na nucleated on the Cu electrode when the deposition capacity reached to 0.5 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, and plenty of obvious dendrites grow larger and larger with the capacity reached to 2 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. During the stripping process, plenty of isolated “dead” dendritic Na are stacked on the planar Cu electrode. Therefore, large quantity of dead deposited Na metal is hardly reversely stripped, leading to a low CE of 67.25% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24g</a>, Supporting Information). For the 3DP rGO electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information), Na metals are nucleated on the rGO electrode and gradually filled the macropores between the rGO nanoflakes when the plating capacity is increased from 0.5 to 2 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. During the stripping process, there are still a few Na metals residual on the rGO nanoflakes. In contrast, during the multiple plating/stripping process, the surface of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode always keeps dendrite-free morphology as shown in the low magnification images. In the enlarged SEM images, Na metal gradually undergoes nucleation and growth on the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO nanoflakes. After stripping process, Na metal gradually diminishes until distinct Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO nanoflakes emerges when the stripping capacity reached to 2 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. Since almost all Na metals are stripped, the CE of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode is as high as ≈100% as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26g</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>The local current density of the electrode was simulated by COMSOL Multiphysics as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4d–f</a>. “Hot spots” is clearly observed on the 2D planar Cu surface, which represents a large local current density leading to uneven distribution (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4d</a>). In contrast, the local current density of the 3DP rGO electrode is significantly reduced compared with that on Cu surface due to the enlarged surface area (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4e</a>). According to the Sand's time formula, dendrite nucleation time is inversely proportional to the square of the local current density.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0057_R_d107712164e1696" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Nat. Commun.">57</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0058_R_d107712164e1696" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Adv. Energy Mater.">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, dendrite-free morphology is easily formed at the electrode with large surface area. However, there are still some “hotspots” on the rGO nanoflakes due to the defects or folds, with the sodiophobicity nature of the rGO nanoflakes require high nucleation overpotential, the dendrites are easily formed at large current conditions. In contrast, the current density of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode is more uniform than that of the 3DP rGO electrode due to the assistant of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4f</a>). In order to explore the sodiophilicity of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>, the binding energy between Na ions and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> was simulated by density functional theory (DFT) calculation. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4g–i</a>, the binding energies of Na ions with functional groups (─F and ─O) of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> are −1.98 and −2.53&nbsp;eV, respectively, which are dramatically higher than of carbon atoms on graphene (−0.06&nbsp;eV) and on Cu (−1.214 to −1.567&nbsp;eV) in previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0042_R_d107712164e1730" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Nano">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, the deposition stability of Na atoms on pure Nb<sub>2</sub>CO were determined by using the <i>ab</i>-initial molecular dynamics (AIMD) simulation with a time step of 1 fs and a total simulation time of 100&nbsp;ps. Clearly, Sodium atoms tend to adsorb on the surface of Nb<sub>2</sub>CO (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0004">4i</a>), forming a 2D diffusion path with a high coefficient of 1.87 × 10<sup>−4</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, hence significantly promoting Na metal deposition kinetics and reversibility. However, Na metal deposition process of C and Cu substrates is unstable from our previous study.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0042_R_d107712164e1751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Nano">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These DFT and AIMD results prove that the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> is sodiophilic due to the abundant ─F and ─O functional groups, and Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes can guide the Na ion uniform deposition, thus leading to low nucleation overpotential and long cycle lifespan.</p>
         
         <p>The excellent electrochemical performance is also determined by the SEI layer formed on the surface of Na metal anodes with the assistant of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes. The SEI compositions with the thickness of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes after cycles were analyzed by in-depth XPS technique at a total depth of 30&nbsp;nm. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0005">5</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a> (Supporting Information) present the deconvoluted XPS spectra of SEI layers formed on the surface of Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO and Na@Cu anodes after 20 cycles at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, respectively. The signals of F 1s, O 1s, and C 1s are gradually changed with the depth of SEI layer (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0005">5a–c</a>). In particular, the corresponding peaks for organic species, such as C─O in O 1s, almost completely disappear above a depth of 10&nbsp;nm, indicating that the organic composition in the SEI layer on both electrodes is greatly reduced. Notably, the organic species of the SEI layer of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode are mainly dispersed in outer layer of SEI, while the inorganic species, such as NaF is increased with the depth of SEI layer, especially in the inner layer of SEI as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0005">5d</a>. In other words, the inner layer of SEI of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO mainly composed of inorganic species especially NaF, while the outer layer of SEI layer is mainly composed of organic species. It is reported that the inorganic NaF is critical for the stable SEI layer to protect the Na metal, enabling the long cycle lifespan.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0014_R_d107712164e1809" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Energy Storage Mater.">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0059_R_d107712164e1809" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Adv. Energy Mater.">59</a>, <a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0060_R_d107712164e1809" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This result is in good consistency with the previous reports.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0042_R_d107712164e1814" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Nano">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the SEI formed in Na@Cu anode has more organics (such as C─C, C─O, and C═O) in inner-SEI (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information), leading to a loosened passivation layer covered on the surface of Na metal, thus causing continuous electrolyte decomposition and poor cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0061_R_d107712164e1823" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202405460-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7022f2ee-603e-4858-a49c-47016d70f1ba/adfm202405460-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7022f2ee-603e-4858-a49c-47016d70f1ba/adfm202405460-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8aed7f18-e792-4702-addc-6b740e4b4323/adfm202405460-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7022f2ee-603e-4858-a49c-47016d70f1ba/adfm202405460-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202405460-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202405460" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Characterization of chemistries of the SEI layer of Na@3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO anode. XPS depth profiles of a) F 1s, b) O 1s, and c) C 1s after 20 cycles at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. d) The content comparison of the organic and inorganic species at different depth. e) Schematic illustration of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO microlattice electrode with hierarchical porous framework to enhance the high performance of Na metal anodes with a stable robust SEI layer.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Based on the aforementioned results, the remarkable electrochemical performance of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO monolith can be attributed to several key advantages (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0005">5e</a>). i) The artificial porous architecture serves as a stable mechanical framework that effectively supports the entire electrode during the repetitive cycling process. ii) The high specific surface area of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode reduces the current density at the electrode surface, thus prolonging the formation time of dendrites, and serving as crucial nucleation sites for sodium nucleation and subsequent electrodeposition.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202405460-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202405460-bib-0062_R_d107712164e1875" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Adv. Sci.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the electrode possesses abundant pores that accommodate the volume changes of sodium metal. iii) The interconnected rGO network, free from binders and additives, ensures high conductivity and facilitates enhanced charge transfer kinetics. iv) The selected Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> nanoflakes have high sodiophilicity, enabling the dendrite-free deposition morphology, as confirmed by various characterization techniques from different scales, such as ex situ SEM from micrometer range, and in situ optical microscopy from submillimeter range. The sodiophilicity of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> is originated from the abundant ─F and ─O functional groups proved by DFT simulation. v) A stable SEI composed of NaF inorganic in the inner layer and organic species at the outer layer on the surface of the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode. Consequently, the incorporation of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene effectively guides the uniform deposition of Na metal, thereby effectively suppressing the growth of Na dendrites and promoting dendrite-free deposition morphology. With the formed stable SEI layer, 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO monolith delivers an ultralong cycle lifespan and exceptional high CE.</p>
         
         <p>To explore the practical application of 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrode, a full cell consisting of a 3DP Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO anode and a 3DP NVP@C/rGO cathode was assembled (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0006">6a</a>). The anode was electrodeposited 2.0 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> Na metal into the 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO to form 3DP Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO anode. The cathode, on the other hand, was prepared by 3D printed NVP@C/rGO with a uniform thickness of 2&nbsp;mm and a mass loading of ≈3.70&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup> (the active mass loading of ≈1.85&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>). At 100&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, the paired 3DP NVP@C/rGO cathode can deliver a remarkable capacity of 87.39 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a> (Supporting Information). The 3DP NVP@C/rGO||Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO full cell, with a N/P ratio of 9.2, could deliver a reversible capacity of 91.83 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the 1st cycle (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0006">6b</a>). Moreover, this full cell also exhibits excellent rate capability as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0006">6c,d</a>. It can deliver discharge capacities of 89.83, 88.82, 81.25, 72.78, and 51.66 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 100, 200, 500, 1000, and 2000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Remarkably, the full cell demonstrates excellent cycling stability, maintaining a high discharge specific capacity of 90.22 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 100&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> over 200 cycles with a low per-cycle decay of 0.009% and a high average CE of 99.54% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202405460-fig-0006">6e</a>).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202405460-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e142ff55-b6f1-45b2-875e-93496b7f5adf/adfm202405460-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e142ff55-b6f1-45b2-875e-93496b7f5adf/adfm202405460-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c8e79b66-f91c-48da-9b74-36b57a2d8573/adfm202405460-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e142ff55-b6f1-45b2-875e-93496b7f5adf/adfm202405460-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202405460-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202405460" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of 3DP NVP@C/rGO||Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO full cell. a) Schematic illustration of the full cell. b) Galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) profiles measured at 100&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. Inset is several LEDs powered by two full cells. c) Rate performance operated at the current densities range of 100–2000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> and d) related GCD profiles. e) Cycling performance and related CE at 100&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202405460-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202405460-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a sodiophilic 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO microlattice monolith electrode was designed and constructed by a direct ink writing technique, and further dedicated as the Na metal host to achieve a long cycle lifespan. The dedicated 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO electrodes exhibit remarkable electrochemical performance, including low nucleation overpotential, high average CE, outstanding cycle stability. For example, 3DP Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO based half-cell can maintain an average CE of 99.68% after cycling for &gt;7064&nbsp;h at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. In the symmetric cell, the Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-30 cell can retain an ultra-long cycle life of 3000&nbsp;h at 1&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. The excellent performance can be not only attributed to the designed 3D architecture with reduced current density and the plenty of micro-cavities to accommodate the Na deposition, but also attributed to the sodiophilic nature of Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> originated from the functional groups which can effectively guide the Na deposition enabling a dendrite free deposition morphology. Furthermore, it is also related to the formed stable SEI layer composed of inorganic NaF in the inner layer and loosely-bound organic species in the outer layers. Finally, the 3DP NVP@C/rGO||Na@Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO full cell exhibits significantly improved cycling performance. This work not only offers a 3D printing strategy to construct sodiophilic MXene matrix to achieve stable Na metal anode, but also provides useful information of the stable SEI layer formed on the Na metal surface with the assistance of the Nb<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub> MXene.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
